## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical kinetics
**Analysis**: This task belongs to the domain of chemical kinetics, specifically focused on modeling the rate of change of concentration in chemical reactions over time. The relationship between concentration and time is a fundamental concept in chemical kinetics.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- First-order kinetics: dA/dt = -k * A (decay with time)
- Second-order kinetics: dA/dt = -k * A**2 (decay with time, non-linear dependence on concentration)
- Zero-order kinetics: dA/dt = -k (constant rate of decay)
- Mass action kinetics: dA/dt = k * A**n * C**(m-n) (complex reaction mechanisms)
- Forward and backward rates: dA/dt = k1 * A**n - k2 * B**(m-n) (net rate of change in concentration)
- Law of mass action: k = k1 * k2 * exp(-Ea/RT) (temperature dependence of reaction rate)
- Arrhenius equation: k = A * exp(-Ea/RT) (temperature dependence of reaction rate)
- Non-catalytic reaction: dA/dt = -k * A**2 (no external factors affecting the reaction rate)
- First-order catalytic reaction: dA/dt = -k * A * C (influence of a catalyst on the reaction rate)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: dA/dt = k * S / (S + K_M) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction with substrate saturation)
- Haldane kinetics: dA/dt = k * A * B / (K_a + A) (reversible reaction with competitive inhibition)
- Washburn equation: A = -r_p * t (adsorption or desorption rate as a function of time)
- Elovich equation: dA/dt = (k * exp(k*t)) / A (diffusion-limited reaction rate)
- Jovanovic-Bajic equation: dA/dt = -k * A / (1 + k * t) (first-order reaction with internal diffusion)
- Non-integer order reaction: dA/dt = -k * A**n (generalized reaction order)
- Weisz-Prisbrey equation: dA/dt = -k * (A / (1 + A^2)) (reaction with non-linear dependence on concentration)
- Vetter equation: dA/dt = -k * (A / sqrt(1 + A^2)) (reaction with non-linear dependence on concentration)
- Second-order with inhibitor: dA/dt = -k * A * B / (B + K_I) (reversible reaction with competitive inhibition)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Decay with time → Exponential decay envelope f(t)*exp(-c*t), Non-integer order reaction dA/dt = -k * A**n (generalized reaction order)
- Concentration dependence → Non-catalytic reaction dA/dt = -k * A**2, Mass action kinetics dA/dt = k * A**n * C**(m-n) (complex reaction mechanisms)
- Non-linear effects → Michaelis-Menten kinetics dA/dt = k * S / (S + K_M) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction with substrate saturation), First-order catalytic reaction dA/dt = -k * A * C (influence of a catalyst on the reaction rate)
- Temperature dependence → Arrhenius equation k = A * exp(-Ea/RT) (temperature dependence of reaction rate), Forward and backward rates dA/dt = k1 * A**n - k2 * B**(m-n) (net rate of change in concentration)
- Sigmoidal behavior → Langmuir-Hinshelwood equation dA/dt = -k * A**2 / (1 + k * A^2) (adsorption with non-linear dependence on concentration)
- Mathematical modeling using classical laws: f(A) = c0 + c1 * A (the relationship between the chemical reaction rate and the reactant concentrations
- Chemical kinetic modeling involving temperature dependency: T * ln(k) = c0 + c1 / T (temperature dependence of reaction rate)
- Chemical kinetic modeling involving multi-reaction system: dA_dt = k1 * A - k2 * B + k3 * C (the relationship between the chemical reaction rate and the reactant concentrations)

Candidates 1-37 (except 38), 39-60: None contain `cos(log(...))` except Candidate 38.

For completeness, let me verify candidates with `sin` terms can't work: `sin(c*A + c)` is periodic in A with constant period, while `cos(log(A+1))` has a period that changes with A. These are fundamentally different functions and cannot be equal for all A ≥ 0.
